The foregoing return shows that the total actual attendances at the Vestry and Committee Meetings combined, from 24th May, 1898, to 16th May, 1899, have been 2,608 out of a possible 4,487, which gives a percentage of 58.12. The actual attendances at Vestry Meetings alone have been 864 out of a possible 1,225, a percentage of 70.53. Of the various Standing Committees, the Works Committee shows the highest actual attendance, viz.: 361, with a percentage of 51.35. The Public Health and Sewers Committee comes next, the actual attendances amounting to 332, which yields a percentage of 48.54. The Finance Committee then follows with an actual attendance of 279, and a percentage of 64.58, while the General Purposes, Trees and Open Spaces Committee shows an actual attendance of 256, and a percentage of 56.88. Special Committees grouped together show an actual attendance of 242, with a percentage of 44.32, and Subcommittees an actual attendance of 274, and a percentage of 57.44. Vestry of St. George the Martyr. southwark. ANNUAL REPORT for the YEAR ENDING 25th MARCH, 1899. IN accordance with the provisions of the Metropolis Local Management Acts, the Vestry presents the following Annual Report for the twelve months ending 25th March, 1899. The following meetings have been held throughout the year. Vestry Meetings 25 Standing Committee Meetings 122 Special Committee ,, 35 Sub-Committee ,, 64 246 PERSONAL. At the first meeting of the newly-elected Vestry on the 24th May, 1898, before proceeding to the ordinary business of the evening, the Vestry passed a resolution expressing their profound regret at the death of the Eight. Hon. William Ewart Gladstone, recording their deep sense of the loss sustained by the nation in his decease, and at the same time expressing their sincere condolence with the widow and family of the deceased statesman in their bereavement. The flag was hung on the Vestry Hall half-mast high, and the offices were closed on Saturday, the 28th May, 1898, being the day of Mr, Gladstone's funeral. 12 Mr. Thomas Haynes was re-appointed Chairman of the Vestry for the year. On the 18th October, 1898, the Yestry passed a vote of condolence with the widow of the late Mr. J. Calver, who was for many years a Member of the Vestry. COMPOUNDING FOR RATES. In consequence of the Vestry having adopted a new scale for Compounding Bates, it became necessary to pass a resolution rescinding an Order of the Vestry of the 14th September, 1869, applying Section 4 of the Poor Bate Collection and Assessment Act, 1869, to this parish. The rescinding resolution was adopted at the meeting of the Vestry on the 5th April, 1898, and came into effect six months after that date. UNDERGROUND CONVENIENCES. Some little delay occurred at the commencement of the year in obtaining the sanction of the Local Government Board for the loan of £3,900, required to carry out the work of constructing the Underground Conveniences in Old Kent Boad and St. George's Circus and the Underground Urinal at the Newington Causeway end of the Borough Boad. The sanction was, however, received on the 5th April, and the Vestry's seal was ordered to be affixed to the mortgage to the Council on the 3rd May. At the meeting of the Vestry on the 7th June, it was determined to invite tenders for the construction of the Conveniences in St. George's Circus and Borough Boad, and, at the same meeting, the seal of the Vestry was affixed to Messrs. .Pinch's contract for the Old Kent Boad Convenience. That firm also obtained the contract for constructing the Convenience at St. George's Circus at the price of £1,659, and the Urinal at the Newington Causeway end of the Borough Boad for £879. No provision was made in the Convenience at St. George's Circus for Females; but on the 28th June the Yestry passed a resolution to the effect that a Women's Convenience be erected at the rear of the Library Buildings, in accordance with the plan then subminitted. An agreement was entered into with the Library ommissioners for the use of the site at the rental of £5 per annum, 13 and the Surveyor was instructed to obtain tenders for the work, The tender of Messrs. Smith & Sons, at the sum of £336, was subsequently accepted, and the work is now proceeding. The construction of the Old Kent Road Convenience was completed about the commencement of February, 1899, when the District Surveyor certified the structure. Attendants were appointed, and the Convenience was handed over to the Public Health Committee, and opened on the 27th February. The Conveniences in St. George's Circus and Borough Road were completed and handed over to the Public Health Committee on the 13th March, 1899. REMAINS IN ST GEORGES CHURCH CRYPT. At the meeting of the Public Health Committee on the 25th April, 1898, the Medical Officer of Health reported that, as desired by the Rector, he had made an examination of the Crypt of St. George's Church, and found that there were a large number of coffins and human remains in the Crypt. He also found the air was musty and unhealthy, particularly at the end of the Crypt, where he discovered cracks in the structure, about half-an-inch wide, which not only rendered the Church dangerous by allowing effluvia to escape into the building, but possibly rendered the Church a dangerous structure. He further stated that, in his opinion, as Medical Officer of Health, the condition of the Crypt was in a state dangerous to health. The question came before the Vestry on the 3rd May, when a resolution was adopted referring the question as to the condition of the Crypt being dangerous, to the Public Health Committee, with power to act. In accordance with this resolution the Committee on the 9th May, requested Dr. Pakes, the Assistant Bacteriologist of Guy's Hospital, to take a sample of the air in the Crypt, to be obtained in the centre transept at the westerly end of the nave, and also a sample of the air in the Church on a morning before the congregation had assembled, and to analyse the samples and report thereon to the Committee. On the 19th May, Dr. Hoffman of the Burial Acts Department of the Home Office attended at St. George's Church to inspect the 14 Crypt, when a letter was read from Dr. Pakes giving the chemical analyses of the air in the Crypt and in the Church, showing that these airs were purely normal. Dr Pakes's formal report was received and submitted to the Vestry on the 24th May, from which it appeared that Carbon dioxide was found to be present in the Church to the extent of only 0.404 parts per thousand parts of air, which would compare favourably with some of the best air in London. The air in the Crypt contained 1.206 parts of Carbon-dioxide per thousand parts of air. The bacteriological analyses showed that the number of organisms per cubic metre found in the Church was 22,000, but apart from a few moulds, a fair number of oidia, a considerable number of torn Ice, no organs resembling any of the common pathogenic ones could be discovered. In the Crypt 16,500 organisms per cubic metre were found. Four-fiths consisted of moulds, oidia, torulas and parcinse; the remaining one-fith consisted of bacteria, among which no pathogenic bacteria could be discovered. In the opinion of the Vestry this report showed that there was no cause for the interference of the Home Office, and a copy of the report was accordingly directed to be forwarded to the Home Secretary. On the 28th June, a letter was read to the Vestry from the Home Office, stating that the Home Secretary had decided to advise the Queen in Council, to make an Order for the removal of the human remains from the Crypt. A resolution was then adopted by the Yestry that, "as the elected Representatives of the Parishioners of St. George the Martyr, Southwark," they regretted the action taken by the Home Secretary with regard to the Crypt, without first giving the Sanitary Authority of the District, an opportunity of being heard, and requested that a Deputation from the Yestry on the subject should be received by the Secretary of State. A further letter was received from the Home Office, asking for the observations of the Vestry upon the question, before the Home Secretary decided whether he would or would not receive the Deputation. Tothis letter the "Vestry replied by a communication pointing out that in their opinion the length and period which had elapsed since 15 any bodies were buried precluded any danger to public health existing or likely to exist, and suggesting that the difficulty might be overcome by the whole surface of the Crypt being sealed with a layer of concrete ; also pointing out that as a large number of bodies are interred beneath the floor of the Crypt, and cracks have appeared in the walls of the Church, there was grave reason to fear that any excavation might tend to weaken the foundation of the building and threaten the stability of the superstructure, but that a layer of concrete would probably bind the structure together. The Home Secretary replied that after considering the representations contained in the letter, he did not find any sufficient grounds to alter his decision and did not think that any advantage would result from a Deputation. The Vestry replied to the communication, regretting the Home Secretary's action, and not only as a Sanitary Authority, but in their capacity as representatives of the ratepayers, again urged upon him the desirability of permitting them to place their arguments before him by deputation. On the 20th September the Home Secretary replied that he saw no reason to vary his decision. On the 25th January, 1899, the Churchwardens discovered a letter in one of the lower rooms of the New Alley premises, adjoining the Churchyard, addressed to them, and containing an Order in Council, made on the 9th August, 1898, directing the whole of the human remains lying in the Crypt to be removed and forthwith interred in some consecrated burial ground in which burials could be legally made—the work of removal to be carried out under the supervision of the Medical Officer of Health of the district. The Under Secretary of State subsequently appointed the 24th February to receive a deputation from the Vestry to discuss the question. The deputation urged upon him the desirability of delaying the removal of the bodies till the proposed Long Lane Improvement is carried out, when other bodies buried in the Churchyard will have to be removed by the London County Council. The Yestry are now awaiting a communication on the matter. TELEPHONES. On the 24th May, 1898, a communication was received from the Clerk to the London County Council, stating that as the question of 16 the London Telephone Service had been referred by the House of Commons to a Select Committee for enquiry,'the Council proposed to hold a Conference of the Metropolitan Local Authorities, on the subject, so as to prepare evidence to lay before the Committee. The Conference was fixed for Tuesday, the 14th June, and delegates were accordingly appointed by the Vestry. Evidence was subsequently given before the Select Committee by representatives of the County Council Conference, and the question stood over to the ensuing Session of Parliament. With regard to the relationships between the National Telephone Company and this Vestry, it may be well to state the action taken by the two bodies:— On the 28th June, 1898, the Vestry passed a resolution directing that six months' notice be given to the National Telephone Company, Limited, to remove the cables laid in Marshalsea Road, in accordance with the terms of the Agreement with the Company; and notice was given accordingly. At the next meeting, the Vestry called the attention of the Company to the inconvenience caused, and the seriousness of the delay, in consequence of the Sanitary Officials being unable to communicate promptly by telephone with the Metropolitan Asylums Board, in cases of infectious disease requiring removal to hospital. At the request of the Telephone Company, the District Manager, had an interview with the Electric Lighting and Dust Disposal Committee of the Vestry, on the 23rd September, and requested that the notice with regard to the Marshalsea Road should be withdrawn, and that the Vestry would consent to the laying of telephone wires in Old Kent, Waterloo, Westminster Bridge, and Borough Roads. Atter volunteering certain information on behalf of the Company, he was requested to supply numerous other particulars, more especially as to the arrangements made between the Company and the other I arishes in the Metropolis. On the basis of the information thus supplied, the Committee recommended the Vestry to consider any offer from the Company, based upon the way-leave granted by the parish of St. Martin's-in-the-Fields to the Company, for which £15 per annum and £1 per 100 feet is paid. The Company declined to accept the offer of the Vestry, but offered to pay 2s. per 17 100 yards of cable laid, and to be subject to certain other conditions laid down by the Vestry. It was, however, determined to adhere to the previous resolution, and at the end of the year no further action had been taken by the Company with reference to the matter. In September, 1898, a letter was received from the Wandsworth Board of Works, expressing the opiuiou that the Telephone Service should be exclusively undertaken by the Government, and that it was not desirable that the Service should be undertaken by the London County Council, or by other Local Authorities, and that the Post Office should not undertake the Service in competition with the National Telephone Company. After considering the matter, the Vestry adopted the following resolution:— " That in the opinion of this Vestry the Telephone Service should be undertaken by Government, in competition with the National Telephone Company." In the 1899 Session of Parliament, the National Telephone Company introduced three Bills— (a) Bill No. 1 for the re-constitution of the Company, and for granting them further powers. (b) Bill No. 2 containing simply the provisions for conferring further powers on the Company; and (c) Bill No. 3, an amendment of the Telegraph Act, 1892. The first two Bills failed to comply with the Standing Orders, and the latter—which contained a clause enabling the Company to appeal to the Railway and Canal Commissioners in the event of a Local Authority withholding its consent or attaching any terms and conditions, to which the Company objected, to the placing of wires within its district, either by means of poles along the public roads or underneath any public street—was subsequently withdrawn. The opposition to the measures was organised by means of a conference convened by the Corporation of London, to which the Vestry appointed Delegates. The Vestry also presented petitions against the three Bills. It is understood that the Government intend to introduce a measure dealing with the whole question of telephones in the present Session of Parliament. 18 metropolitan police. Notwithstanding the representations made in 1897 to the Home Office with regard to the inadequacy of the Police Force to deal with the serious crimes committed from time to time in this district, it was found that rowdyism still continued to prevail in South London. The Yestry, on the 26th July, 1898, accordingly passed the following resolutions "That application be made to Parliament to sanction an increased grant to the Police Force, so that adequate Police protection can be secured to persons and property in South London, which at present does not obtain." That this Authority is of opinion that this district is insufficiently provided with police protection and that the prevailing and increased rowdyism, ruffianism, intimidation and number of assaults call for immediate attention and suppression." The resolutions were forwarded to the Home Secretary and the Chief Commissioner of Police. While on the subject of the Police, it may be well to mention that in September, 1898, the Yestry received a communication from the Chief Commissioner, inviting the co-operation of Local Authorities in assisting the Police to devise means for lessening the traffic in busy thoroughfares, and suggesting that main thoroughfares should be watered during the night and the gutters during the day time so as to obviate the slipping of horses. To this communication the Yestry directed a reply to be sent to the effect that:— "(a) That the question of scavenging at night time is now receiving the attention of the Vestry; (b) That watering the streets during the night only is impracticable; (c) That so soon as the improvements at the Elephant and Castle and Long Lane are completed the traffic would be materially lessened at. these points; (d) That more Police are necessary to efficiently regulate the traffic at the Elephant and Castle; (e) That the Commissioner be recommended to approach the London County Council with a view of diverting some of the tramway traffic from London Eoad, down St. George's Ptoad and Lancaster Street; (f) That, in the opinion of the Vestry, the By-laws should be enforced respecting the distance to be maintained between each tramcar. rating of ground values. On the -29th November, 1898, the Vestry considered a letter from the Land Law Reform Association, inviting the Authority to 19 send delegates to a Conference on the question of the rating of ground values. Four Members of the Vestry were accordingly appointed to attend the Conference, which was held at the Westminster Palace Hotel, on the 8th December, 1898. The delegates subsequently reported that resolutions were adopted at the Conference in favour of the rating of ground values, and a Petition was presented to Parliament by the Vestry embodying the decisions of the Conference. london government. The question of the reform of London Government, so far as the various Local Authorities are concerned, having become ripe fur discussion by reason of the declaration of the intention of the Government to introduce a measure dealing with the question, in the succeeding Session of Parliament, a conference was convened by the Vestry of Islington in October, 1898, to consider the whole subject. Representatives of the Yestry were appointed and many of the recommendations agreed to by the Conference, have been subsequently adopted by the Government. On the 1st November, a letter was received from the St. Saviour's Vestry, stating that a Conference would be held on the 2nd inst., respecting the question of the full Incorporation of the Ward of Bridge Without. Delegates were appointed by the Vestry to the Conference with a view of watching the proceedings and to report the result to the Vestry. At the conference certain resolutions were drafted which it was agreed should be submitted by the Representatives of each Vestry to their respective Authorities. The resolutions were reported to the Vestry on the 15th November, 1898, when a Special Committee was appointed to consider and report on the whole subject of the Government of London so far as it affected this parish. The Committee, however, after carefully considering the proposals of the two Conferences above referred to, were unable to agree upon any suggestions laid before them and a Special Meeting of the Vestry in Committee was accordingly convened to further consider the matter for the 20th December, 1898, but in view of the fact that the 20 Government had not yet introduced their measure or indicated its character or scope, it was deemed imprudent to deal with the question till that event had taken place. The promised Bill was introduced by the Rt. Hon. A. J. Balfour, M.P., First Lord of the Treasury, into the House of Commons on the 23rd February, 1899. Prints of the Bill were issued on the 1st March, and on the 3rd of that month, a Special Committee of the Vestry considered the measure, when a large number of recommendations were made to the Vestry. At the Vestry Meeting held on the 7th March, a resolution was passed strongly disapproving of the Bill on the grounds that it did not simplify the administration, that it did not provide for further relief of Local Taxation and that it destroyed many valuable Authorities at present doing excellent administrative work in all parts of London. The Vestry also adopted the following recommendations of the Committee:— 1.—"That in the opinion of the Vestry, the London Government Bill should not be passed into Law, unless the areas of the whole of the proposed Metropolitan Boroughs are included in the first Schedule to the Bill." 2.—"That as far as possible the areas of the new Boroughs should be fixed on the lines of the Poor Law Unions." 3.—"That in the opinion of the Vestry, the constitution of Aldermen as part of the new Councils is contrary to the principle of direct representation, and should be eliminated from the Bill." 4- "That the number of Councillors assigned to each of the Wards of the new Boroughs should be based upon the population, and not on the rateable value." That it should be made clear in the Bill that women are eligible to sit upon, and to hold any office upon the Council. 6.- That it should be provided in the Bill, that the jurisdiction of the City Coiporation and its officials over the ancient Borough of Southwark should be entirely abolished. 7.-Thatin the case of borrowing powers being transferred to the new Councils, the sanction of the London County Council should still be required instead of that of the Local Government Board as provided in the Bill. 8. That theVestry express its disapproval of the provisions contained in Clauses 5 and 8 of the Bill relating to the transfer by the Local Govern- 21 merit Board of the powers of the County Council to a Borough Council, on an agreement being arrived at between the two Councils. 9.—That the words "or of any of their other powers or duties "should be eliminated from Clause 9. 10.—That the words "by a body containing representatives elected by the Guardians "should be omitted from Clause 11, line 39. It remains to be seen how many of these recommendations will be adopted in the Bill. It was at the same meeting determined to invite the four Vestries contained in the St. Saviour's Union, to a Conference to be held on the 17th March, to consider the whole question as to the formation of a suitable area in this district. At that Conference it was found impossible for any other representatives than those of the Parishes of St. George and Christ Church to be present, and after expressing the opinion that the areas outside those mentioned in the Schedule to the Bill should be formed upon Poor Law Union limitations, the Conference adjourned. A further Conference was convened by the St.. Olave's Board of Works suggesting that the whole of the Parliamentary Borough of South'wark should form a Borough Council. This Conference, however, which was held at the Offices of the St. Olave's Board, adjourned without being able to come to any definite determination on the matter. A further amendment to the Bill was adopted by the Vestry at the meeting held on the 21st March, to the effect:— "That the Bill should provide for the powers and duties of Overseers to be transferred direct to the new Councils." The Bill passed the second reading on the 14th March. It is expected that it will be considerably amended in Committee. long lane improvement. Notice to Treat in respect of the portion of the Churchyard proposed to be included in the new road to be constructed by the County Council in extension of Tabard Street, was served on the Vestry on the 5th April, 1898. The Council subsequently applied to be permitted to take immediate possession of the premises in New Alley belonging to the 22 Vestry, and this request was agreed to on the 3rd May, 1898, subject to the Council making arrangements with the tenants now occupying the premises. The Council have not yet taken possession of the property. At the following meeting of the Vestry a resolution was adopted to the effect that, subject to the consent of the Home Secretary being obtained, the Vestry would offer no objection to the proposal to re-inter the human remains from the portion of the Churchyard required for the new road, in the Easterly portion of the Churchyard, provided the Rector and Churchwardens agreed thereto. The Vestry made a claim in respect of the portion of the Churchyard to be taken by the Council under the Notice to Treat, upon the principle of reinstatement instead of a monetary consideration. The claim includes, amongst other conditions, the provision of an open space of equal or greater area than the land taken, and the paving of the new roadway with wood. It was further determined, at the meeting of the Vestry on the 28th June, that the open space should not be used as a playground for children. At the request of the Council, Mr. Douglas Young was appointed as the Surveyor of the Vestry in respect of the two claims for the taking of the New Alley Premises and for the taking of a portion of the Churchyard, but it was deemed inexpedient by the Authority to unite the two claims either on the basis of reinstatement or a monetary consideration. vestry offices. On the 3rd May, 1898, the Yestry adopted a resolution, on the recommendation of a Special Committee, to the effect that in future the time of attendance at the office of all the clerks employed by the Vestry be from 9 in the morning. The time at which the clerks were required to attend at the office was previously 10 a.m., and three months notice was accordingly given to the clerks as to the change of hours. committees' reports. The method of reading the whole of the minutes of the Committees at the Vestry Meeting—a process which occupied a consider able length of time and otten failed to secure adequate consideration for important resolutions—was finally abandoned by the 23 Vestry at the commencement of the summer vacation in 1898, and at the succeeding meeting on the 6th September, Reports of the Committees were for the first time included in the Vestry's Agenda and brought up in printed form in accordance with a resolution adopted on the 28th June, 1898. The writing up of the minutes of the vestry in a minute book was also abandoned on the 18th October, 1898, and printed minutes kept in a binding file, each page being initialled by the Chairman, were substituted therefor. lost assessments. The attention of the vestry was, on the 10th January, 1899, called by the vestry of St. Leonard, Shoreditch, to certain disclosures in the "City Press" of the 12th November, 1898, respecting certain "lost assessments" in the City, and a resolution was passed concurring with the latter Yestry in urging upon the London County Council to take immediate steps to remedy the alleged irregularities. At a subsequent meeting of the Vestry a letter was read from the Clerk of the Council, statiug that the Town Clerk of the City had replied to the Council that the errors were merely omissions from the rate books. labour bureaux. A communication was received from the Vestry of Islington, on the 21st February, 1899, stating that it was proposed to hold a Conference on the subject of Labour Bureaux, and inviting the Vestry to appoint representatives. Delegates were accordingly elected to attend the Conference, which was held on Wednesday, 22nd March, 1899. Reconstruction of Sewers in Friar Street Area. Public Health and Sewers Committee. In the early part of the year 1898, the Surveyor, in accordance with the instructions of the Vestry, submitted a scheme for the re-drainage of the Friar Street and Pocock Street areas, as an instalment of a larger scheme for the re-construction and repair of the whole of the defective sewers throughout the Parish. The estimates of the Surveyor, amounting to £4222 12s. 7d., were adopted by the Vestry on the 5th April, 1898, and 24 application was directed to be made to the London County Council for a loan of £4250, to be taken up on the following 1st October. The Council reduced the amount by £200, which they understood to be establishment charges, and offeied to giant a loan of £4050. This loan was accepted by the Vestry on the 21st July, the conditions of repayment being by annual instalments of principal and interest on the balance outstanding for a period of twenty yeais. The Council subsequently agreed to grant a loan of £200 to defray the cost of the salaries of the Draughtsman and Clerk of Works, if the same were added to the next loan applied for. The Surveyor was instructed to proceed with the work on the 6th September, 1898, and, at the same meeting, the mortgage for the money was sealed by the Vestry. Re-laying of Sewers. A serious case of typhus fever occurred at 20, Toulmin Street, at Typhus Fever.Easter, 1898.during the absence of the Medical Officer on vacation; but, by the prompt and vigorous action of Dr. Smith, who acted as Dr. Waldo's locum tenens, and Dr. Massie, the medical attendant on the patient, every precaution was taken to prevent the spread ot the disease, with great success; and, as a mark of their appreciation of the efforts of the two Doctors, the Vestry passed a resolution on the 15th April, 1898, placing on record their high appreciation of the skill and vigilance displayed by them in thus preventing the spread of the disease. 25 Overcrowding and Housing of the Working Classes. The density of the population on the South side of the river, and the difficulty of obtaining suitable houses for the working classes, induced the Vestry of Bermondsey to convene a Conference on the subject of overcrowding and on the housing of the working classes. The Vestry accordingly appointed delegates to attend the Conference, which was held on the 15th July, 1898, at the Bermondsey Town Hall, when various resolutions were adopted calling upon the London County Council to exercise their power under the Housing of the Working Classes Act, 1890, to provide dwellings within the County of London where required, and suggesting certain alterations of the law and of financial arrangements to enable Local Authorities also to erect municipal dwellings. The resolutions came before the Yestry on the 29th November, when the Vestry expressed its concurrence with the former proposal, and also with proposals that Local Authorities should be allowed to erect and permanently manage dwellings under Part I, Section 12 (5) of the Housing of the Working Classes Act, and that the period of borrowing should be extended to one hundred years, but disagreed with the proposals to enable Metropolitan Local Authorities to erect municipal dwellings under part 3 of the Act. In February, 1898, a letter was received from the St. Saviour's Board of Guardians, drawing attention to the overcrowding within the area of the Union. The matter received the consideration of the Public Health Committee who directed a reply to be sent to the effect that the subject was continually receiving attention by the Committee and the Sanitary Staff, and they felt that every effort was being made to comply with the provisions of the Act for the abatement of overcrowding in the parish, at the same time no tangible suggestion had been laid before the Committee that could be recommended for adoption. Condensed Separated Milk. At the suggestion of the Vestry of Camberwell, the Yestry passed resolutions on the 20th September, 1898, urging the Government to introduce a Bill requiring persons manufacturing or importing condensed milk to state the quantity necessary to obtain the full benefit of new English milk. This resolution, which was adopted by a large number of Authorities 26 throughout the Metropolis, was followed up by the appointment of a deputation to wait on the Board of Agriculture with reference to the subject. Representatives of the Yestry accompanied the deputation, which was received by Mr. Long, of the Board of Agriculture, on Monday the 20th March, 1899. L.C.C. Bacteriological Laboratory On the 20th September, 1898, the Vestry had before them a proposal of the London County Council to establish a Bacteriological Laboratory, with a view to aiding Medical Officers of Health and medical practitioners in the diagnosis of suspected cases of infectious disease at the expense of the County, when a resolution was adopted expressing the opinion that the Council should apply for power to establish such a department. Sterilised Tubes for Bacteriological Examination. The question of providing gratuitously sterilised tubes to medical practitioners for bacteriological examinations in doubtful cases of infectious disease was considered by the Public Health Committee at considerable length, the matter being adjourned from time to time, in order that the Committee might, if possible, be furnished with further evidence as to the advantages of the system. They, however, were eventually unable, from the evidence laid before them, to see their way to recommend the adoption of the system by the Vestry. Red Cow Alley.. At the meeting of the Vestry on the 18th October, a formal resolution was passed to the effect that the continuance of the premises Nos. 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5, Red Cow Alley was dangerous or injurious to the health of the inhabitants of the neighbouring dwelling-houses, and that it was expedient to order the demolition of the same. Tuesday, the 29th November was fixed for further consideration of the resolution, and on that date a representative of the owners attended the Vestry, and stated that he could not say that the owners were prepared to put the property into a proper state of repair They objected to demolition on the grounds that the premises were not dangerous, and failed to see the right of the Vestry to order their demolition. The Vestry, however, made an Order for the demolition of the premises. 27 Messrs. Gover, the owners of the houses, gave notice of appeal to the Quarter Sessions, and the Vestry determined to defend their Order. The Appeal came before the Court of Quarter Sessions at Newington on the 13th January, 1899, when, after hearing evidence on behalf of both parties, the Court decided that the premises were in such a condition as to be dangerous or injurious to the health of the surrounding population, and the public generally. They, however, came to the conclusion that in Section 33, Part II. of the Housing of the Working Classes Act, 1890, the word "dwelling-house" meant an inhabited dwelling-house in accordance with the definition contained in Section 29. The Court thereupon decided that as the Act was a penal one, they must read it strictly, and that Section 33 must be taken to refer to an inhabited house only, and as the houses referred to were not then inhabited, but in a ruinous state, they accordingly quashed the order. The Chairman, however, expressed the willingness of the Court to state a Case for the decision of the High Court on the point of law thus raised, and the Vestry determined to adopt this course. The case has been drafted by Mr. Corrie Grant on behalf of the Vestry, and is now in the hands of Messrs. Gover's solicitors for approval. Addresses of Outworkers. The Yestry of St. Mary, Battersea, having suggested inter-communication between Sanitary Authorities for the inter-change 'of information relative to outworkers, the Vestry passed a resolution concurring with the Authority in the proposal. It was deemed, however, to be impracticable to put the suggestion into practice, owing to the want of a complete list of streets in each of the parishes throughout the Metropolis, showing the number of houses in each respective parish. A resolution was therefore adopted, directing a communication to be forwarded to the London County Council, suggesting the advisability of the Council preparing a complete list of the whole of the streets in the Metropolis, showing, in respect of streets in more than one parish, the numbers of the houses in each respective parish. The question has been brought before the Council, but, up to the present, they have been unable to see their way to have such a list compiled. 28 Occupation of Underground Rooms. By Section 96 of the Public Health (London) Act, 1891, the occupation of underground rooms not occupied in conjunction with any other room or rooms on any other floor of the same house is forbidden. In the case of underground rooms let in connection with premises on another floor no such prohibition exists. The Committee found that in a considerable number of cases throughout the parish underground rooms let in connection with rooms on other floors were occupied for sleeping purposes. They accordingly directed the Medical Officer of Health to report on the best means of preventing such underground rooms being used for this purpose. The Medical Officer suggested that the desired object might be obtained by deleting the word "separately" from Sub. Section 1 of Section 96 of the Public Health (London) Act, 1891. A communication was accordingly directed to the Local Government Board, urging that a Clause should be inserted in any Bill promoted for the amendment of the Public Health (London) Act, 1891, amending Section 96 accordingly. Establishment of Public Slaughterhouses and Abattoirs. In November, 1899, a proposal came before the London County Council to abolish private slaughter-houses and establish public slaughter-houses and abattoirs throughout the Metropolis. The suggestion was strongly opposed by many Authorities and the Vestry received communications from the London Butchers' Trade Society and the London Chamber of Commerce, urging them to join in the opposition to the scheme. The matter came before the Vestry on the 29th November, when a resolution was adopted to the effect, that, in their opinion no adequate reasons had been adduced for the abolition of private slaughter-houses for the purpose of establishing the proposed costly and extensive public abattoirs. The Vestry further declined to support any proposition for the establishment of public abattoirs. Flooding of Basements. About Christmas, 1898, several heavy rain storms occurred which caused the flooding of basements in various parts of the parish, owing to the main sewers of the London County Council being inadequate to carry off the storm water. 29 It was reported to the Vestry, that in 1895 the Medical Officer of Health sent to the Chairman of the Main Drainage Committee of the Council a list of 20 cases of sewage flooding in basements, and in many of the instances referred to the rooms were used as work, rooms, but no action had yet been taken by the Council to deal with the matter in this district. A communication was accordingly directed to be forwarded to the London County Council drawing attention to the serious possible consequences that may arise from flooding of basement rooms, and urgently requesting the Council to take immediate steps for more efficiently dealing with storm water. The matter again came before the Vestry on the 7th February, 1899, upon a report by the Committee of the result of the Surveyor's inspection of certain arrangements at premises in Old Kent Road to prevent the flooding of basements. The Committee expressed the opinion that the' particular trap used, which is on the "stop back" valve principle, would doubtless prevent flooding, provided the drain is thoroughly well laid in a good bed of not less than six inches of concrete. Directions were given to the Inspectors in the event of a recur, rence of flooding to take the necessary steps by the service of intimations and notices to abate the nuisance and prevent a recurrence thereof, and to take proceedings if the notices were not complied with. A letter was also received by the Vestry from the Local Government Board on the subject, and a reply was directed to be sent by the Vestry Clerk to inform the Board of the steps taken by the Authority in drawing the attention of the Council to the matter, and of the above course adopted by the Vestry. Phthisis. At the meeting of the Vestry on the 7th February, 1899, a resolution was adopted to the effect, that seeing much suffering and a large number of deaths arise from phthisis, it being an infectious disease, the Medical Officer of Health be desired to point out in simple language, the danger of the disease, and to draft regulations which should be observed in respect to its prevention, 30 The question of tuberculosis also came before the Vestry at the meeting on the 21st March, on a letter from the Vestry of Westminster, drawing attention to the frequency with which milk and cream are infected with tubercle bacilli, and to the spread of this disease through this medium. A resolution was adopted by the authority directing that representation be made to the Board of Agriculture and the Local Government Board pointing out the necessity and advisability of so varying the provisions of the Dairies, Cowsheds and Milkshops Order, 1885, as to make it include the case of a cow with disease of the udder, which shall have been certified by a veterinary surgeon to be suffering from tubercular disease, and further that any cow found to be suffering from tuberculous disease should be condemned to be slaughtered, and such parts destroyed as shall be considered unfit for human food and dangerous to health if so used, and suggesting that compensation should be paid to the owner, provided that at the time of seizure the animal was of no less value than £10. Female Sanitary Inspector. The advisability of appointing an additional Female Inspector came before the Vestry on the 21st March, 1899, on a report from the Committee that very successful work had been carried out by the present Inspector with regard to houses let in lodgings, and the Medical Officer of Health reported that there was still a large number of houses in the parish which could be registered under the Tenement Bye-Laws. The Vestry determined to appoint an additional female Sanitary Inspector at a salary of £110 per annum rising by annual increments to a maximum of £150, subject to the approval of the Local Government .Board. Loan of ill,100. Works Committee. Early in the year 1898, it was determined to erect new workshops at the King James Street Yard, in accordance with plans and estimates which had been prepared by the Surveyor, at an estimated cost ot £350. On the 3rd May, 1898, resolutions were adopted for paving the portion of the carriage-way in the Waterloo Road, opposite the Board School, and also the portion of the c arnage-way ot Borough Boad, opposite the Library, with Jarrah wood blocks, the net estimated cost amounting to £293, 31 At the next meeting, the asphalting of the carriage-way in Union Street was added to the work, and it was then determined to apply to the London County Council for a loan of .£1,100, to include the above work. The sum of £200 was also added, being the amount deducted by the Council from the loan for sewerage works, thus making the total amount asked for £1,300. On application being made to the London County Council, some correspondence took place between the Vestry and the Council with regard to the loan, from which the Council insisted on deducting £57 9s. 0d., on the ground that they considered 12s. per yard was sufficient for the wood and asphalte paving, whereas the Vestry's late Surveyor and the present Surveyor stated that it was utterly impossible to carry out the work at less than 13s. Od. per yard. The Council also asked interest at 3£ per cent., a rate of interest which the Committee considered was more than ought to be paid, and after further correspondence the loan was abandoned. l. c. c. By-Laws as to Lamps, Ac. In May, 1898, the County Council forwarded to the Vestry, draft By-Laws for the regulation of lamps, signs and other structures overhanging the public way. After considering the By-Laws the Vestry made certain amendments therein, and returned them to the Council. The chief objection was raised to By-Law No. 19, which proposed to empower the Council, in any case which it might consider expedient, to modify or dispense with the observance of the By-Law on such terms and conditions as it might think proper. As the By-Laws were to be administered by the Local Authority, the Vestry expressed strong disapproval of this proposal as contrary to the spirit of the Section under which the By-Laws were framed. Dusting and Scavenging. An important report was brought before the Vestry on 29th November, 1898, by the Committee, containing suggestions from the Surveyor for extensive alterations in the present method of dealing with the work of dusting and scavenging, so as to secure the same being done more efficiently and frequently. The principal alterations consisted of the establishment of an early morning gang for scavenging the principal streets, the commencement of the horse brooms at 3 a.m. instead of 6 a.m., and the making 32 of the gangs to a certain extent common, in order to enable tne General Foreman to find work for dust trounoers during the time the vans are away at the shoot. The suggestions provided for the scavenging daily of all the principal roads in the parish, and of several of the side streets in Wards 1 and 2 twice a week, and Ward 3 three times a week. It also insured, as far a possible, the clearing of the dust from every place in the parish, twice a week. Numerous alterations in the staff were required, but the change was carried out, and is now working with very little friction. Street Lighting. An important offer was made to the Vestry in March, 1899, by the South Metropolitan Gras Company, for introducing a new design of lanterns and substituting incandescent burners for the present ones, in a large number of lamps throughout the parish. The proposal is still under the consideration of the Vestry. Asphalting Streets. As there was a large quantity of work to be carried out, it was determined that the concrete foundations should be prepared by the Vestry's workmen and the asphalte laid by a contractor. The A estry received a communication from the Yestry of St. Mary, Battersea, asking support to resolutions of that Authority requesting the London County Council to adopt regulations with regard to District Surveyors, providing that they should devote the whole of their time to the duties, that they 33 should be paid a salary, and all building fees be paid to the Council, and that their offices should be at the Local Vestry Hall, so that they might be brought into closer touch with the Local Authorities. After considering the matter, the Vestry passed a resolution concurring with the views of the Battersea Vestry. The Paragon. General Purposes Committee. The necessary documents for the completion of the purchase of the Paragon Ground having been prepared, the Vestry, on the 7th June, 1898, directed a cheque to be drawn for the purchase-money, £3,400. It was, however, then found that the builder, who was engaged in taking down the old houses at the Paragon, had used the open space as a depository for building materials of all kinds, and, under the circumstances, the Vestry deemed it advisable to defer the purchase until the space was cleared. The purchase was completed on the 13th September, 1898, and at the meeting of the Vestry on the 18th October, permission was given to the Metropolitan Public Gardens Association to proceed with the work of laying out the ground, the plans having been previously approved by the Vestry. The work is now proceeding rapidly, the Vestry having accepted tenders for the provision of the necessary gates, railings and iron fencing, and arranged for a suitable water supply to be provided. It is hoped the ground will be opened soon after Whitsuntide. Portland Place open space. On the 24th July, 1898, the Vestry received a letter from the Metropolitan Public Gardens Association stating that the Trustees of St. Bartholomew's Hospital were prepared to grant a lease to the Vestry of the triangular piece of ground opposite Portland Terrace for a term of eighty years, at a rental of 1s. per annum, and that the Association were prepared to lay out the piece of ground in the event of the lease being obtained and subject to the Vestry maintaining the ground, and providing and fixing new iron railings opposite the houses in Portland Terrace. The lease of the ground was completed on the 25th October, 1898, and the Association are now carrying out the work of planting the ground and making the footpaths, and the Vestry of fixing the new iron railings, and making and fixing new iron gates, &c. 34 Parapet Walls on High Buildings. In the month of June, 1898, a fatal accident occurred to a man who fell from the roof of Queen's Buildings, and the attention of the authority was thus called to the danger arising from high buildings of this character not being surrounded by more efficient protection on the parapet walls of the roofs to prevent accidents of this kind occurring; at the same time the attention of the Vestry was drawn to the fact that owing to the lack of such protection, boys not infrequently ran along the parapet walls of Queen's Buildings to their great risk and danger. The Vestry accordingly deemed it desirable to call the attention of the County Council to the necessity of more efficient protection being provided, and suggested the advisability for that authority obtaining statutory powers, enabling them to deal with these cases. A communication was received from the Council in regard to this recommendation, stating that the Building Act Committee were unable to see their way to recommend the Council to obtain statutory authority to compel owners of model dwellings of considerable height to provide such protection. The Vestry, on the 13th December, 1898, in view of another accident which had occurred in the meantime, at the same building, directed a reply to be sent to this communication asking the Building Act Committee of the Council to reconsider the subject and embody a clause in the direction indicated, in any General Powers Bill the Council was likely to promote in the ensuing Session of Parliament. It is much to be regretted that the Council have not seen their way to take this course. Control of Open Spaces. The question of the control of the smaller Open Spaces throughout the Metropolis having come before the London County Council, they determined to convene a conference on the matter, and at their request the Vestry appointed delegates thereto. The conference was held at the County Hall, Spring Gardens, on Wednesday the 25th January, 1899, when a resolution was adopted to the effect that the maintenance and control of all Open Spaces under ten acres should be undertaken by the Sanitary Authority for the District, and that the Council should grant to the Authority the amount of the cost, 35 based upon the average expenditure on the Open Space for the preceding three years; the grant to be subject to a certificate of the Council's officials that the expense has been incurred and the work properly carried out. South Eastern and London, Ghatham, and Dover Railway. A Bill was promoted by the South Eastern Eailway Company and the London, Chatham and Dover Railway Company, for the amalgamation of the two Companies by means of a joint committee to manage the whole system. It was felt generally throughout the Metropolis that the effect of such- an amalgamation would, by destroying competition, tend to increase tariffs on the two lines. A number of Authorities accordingly determined to petition against the Bill, and on the 21st February, 1899, the Vestry also decided to present a petition against the measure. The Bill has not yet come before a Parliamentary Committee. On the recommendation of the General Purposes Committee, the Yestry expressed the following opinions on the under-mentioned matters:— Shops Bill, 1898. On the suggestion of the Vestry of Limehouse, the Vestry passed a resolution concurring with the views of that Authority that the Bill should not become Law. L. C. C. Parliamentary Agent. On the suggestion of the Yestry of St. Mary, Battersea, the Yestry concurred in the opinion that the London County Council should have the whole services of their Parliamentary Agent. Combined Drainage. A Bill was promoted by a conference of Metropolitan Local Authorities which met from time to time at the Holborn Town Hall, for the purpose of drafting a measure calculated to relieve the Metropolitan Authorities from the burden thrown upon them by recent decisions, of repairing what are in fact private drains as public sewers. The Bill proposed to alter the definition of the word "drain" in the Metropolis Management Acts, so as to include any drain, the construction of which as a sewer has not been 36 sanctioned by a Local Authority, or which has not been approved as a sewer by the Commissioners of Sewers, the Metropolitan Board of Works, or the London County Council. The Vestry concurred with the provisions of the Bill, and urged the London County Council to take up and secure the introduction of the measure. Census. The Vestry concurred with the expression of opinion of the Vestry of Camberwell that Her Majesty's Government should be asked to provide for the future taking of the Census in the Metropolis by the same authority that is responsible for the preparation of the Voters lists, having regard to the great importance of a correct return being obtained for the equitable working of the Equalisation of Kates Act. Inter-communication by underground electric railways. The Vestry of St. Margaret and St. John, Westminster, urged upon the Vestry to support that authority in making representation to the London County Council to oppose certain underground electric railway schemes with a view to the formation of a Parliamentary Committee to consider and report upon the routes along which further underground electric railways should pass, so that such schemes should be based upon a considered and formulated plan of inter-communication throughout London to be defined by Parliament. The Vestry concurred with this view and directed a communication to be forwarded to the London County Council accordingly. Rating of railways in progress. The attention of the Vestry was called by the Vestry of St. Mary, Lattersea, to the necessity of a measure being passed to amend Section 133 of the Lands Clauses Consolidation Act, 1845, whereby local authorities shall in future be entitled to be recouped the whole of the local rates instead of only the Poor Late in respect of any property acquired by railway or other companies until the new works come into rating. The Vestry concurred with this view, and directed a communication to be forwarded to the local Members of Parliament accordingly. 37 Central Electric Supply Company. A Bill was promoted by this Company to enable them to supply electricity in bulk to various electric supply companies throughout the Metropolis, including amongst others, the London Electric Supply Corporation, which supplies electrical energy in this parish. The Bill was an attempt to render useless the powers of local authorities to purchase electric lighting undertakings in their respective parishes by reducing the undertakings to mere sets of wires without generating stations ; but as the place where it was proposed to establish the central station was Marylebone, the locus standi of the other parishes was not admitted. An attempt was made to throw out the Bill on Second Reading, but this was not successful. It is satisfactory to know that the name of the Company supplying this Parish was omitted in the House of Lords. Streets Traffic Bill. A Bill was promoted by the Chief Commissioner of Police with a view to empower him to regulate the character of the traffic along any of the streets and roads of the Metropolis. It was felt that this power might lead to invidious distinctions being made betweeu different kinds of traffic, which might produce great inconvenience to tradesmen and others. A strong feeling was expressed that the Bill ought not to pass into law, and the Vestry petitioned against it in the House of Commons. The Bill was subsequently dropped by the Government. Charities Committee. United Charities Scheme. On the 6th September, the Committee presented a report to the Vestry upon a draft scheme received by them from the Charity Commissioners, for the future regulation of certain of the charities of the parish. The scheme contained a proposal to constitute a body of thirteen Trustees— seven to be elected by the Vestry, five co-optative Trustees (including two life Trustees), and the Rector as an ex-officio Trustee—to whom the whole management and control of the charities referred to should be committed, and it was provided that, after applying the necessary amounts towards Sir John Fenner's and Edward Martin's charities in the purchase and distribution of bibles, and the educational purposes of Delaforce's Charity, the balance of the residue of the income of the charities should be applied in the 38 payment of pensions of not less than 7s. per week or more than 10s. per week, and provisions were made for the election of the pensioners accordingly. The Committee made several recommendations for the amendment of the scheme, the principal of which were as follows:— They asked that Humphrey Williams' (Kent Street) Charity and Simmonds's Charity should be included in the scheme. They opposed the appointment of five co-optative Trustees' as inconsistent with the Trusts under which the various charities were constituted. They suggested the increase of the number of Trustees to 22, and, if a less number, no ex-officio members to be included. They further suggested that the amount applicable in the purchase of bibles should be reduced to £5. A strong opposition was shown to a clause compelling the Trustees to apply a yearly sum of £300 towards the provision of nurses and temporary relief. It was also suggested that a clause should be inserted in the scheme protecting the rights of the present pensioners. The Vestry agreed to these recommendations, and appointed a Deputation to wait upon the Charity Commissioners to fully place the views of the Vestry before them. Sir Henry Longley, K.C.B., Chief Commissioner, received the Deputation on Thursday, the 24th November, 1898, when he stated, in dealing with the amendments suggested by the Vestry, that in appointing co-optative Trustees, the Commissioners had only followed their usual practice, but they would be prepared to consider other names, to be suggested by the Vestry, in the place of those mentioned in the scheme, as co-optative Trustees, for five years. With regard to the two life Trustees, the gentlemen being old Trustees, had made it a condition of their assent to the scheme, that they should be so appointed, which the Commissioners agreed to. The Commissioner also pointed out that although the Charity Commissioners were desirous of altering the application of the funds of the Bible Charities, the Court of Chancery had in a similar case decided that this could not be done without a special Act of Parliament. He agreed to the substitution of "may" for "shall" in the clause as to the sum ot £300 being applied for the provision of nurses and to the omission ot the Sub-section as to temporary relief, thus leaving it optional to the trustees to make a grant for the provision 39 of nurses for the sick and aged poor. He also agreed to a clause protecting the rights of the present pensioners. Sir Henry Longley added that it was intended to deal with Humphry Williams and Simmonds Charities by a further scheme. The original scheme was completed and sealed by the Charity Commissioners on the 21st March, 1899, and included in the names of the co-optative Trustees was one nominated by the Vestry in place of one named by the Commissioners, who declined to act. The number of Trustees remain as originally fixed at thirteen, but the other clauses have been altered as agreed to by Sir Henry Longley. Application for Revocation of Provisional Order. Electric Lighting and Dust Disposal Committer. county ok london and brush provincial electric lighting company. The position taken by the Board of Trade in the early part of 1808, of refusing to revoke the Order of the County of London and Brush Provincial Electric Lighting Company, on the ground that the Company had not carried out its Order for the period of six years, was maintained by the Board. The plans of the Company having been disapproved by the Vestry and the County Council, the Company appealed to the Board of Trade, who appointed Major Cardew, Inspector of the Board, to hold an inquiry with reference to the matter. The Inquiry was held on the 27th June, 1808, when the Vestry were represented by Counsel (Mr. Corrie Grant), the Company by Mr. Sydney Morse, their Solicitor, and Mr. A. J. Lawson, their Engineer, and the Council by the Chairman of the Highways Committee and other Members. After hearing the arguments on both sides, the Inspector made an award on the 11th July, allowing the appeal of the Company, upon conditions that they gave a written consent to the Board of Trade that they would at once commence and diligently proceed with the execution of the works, and that, if within eighteen months from the date of the Order they were unable to give a supply of energy in the parish from any generating station, they would at once proceed to ereet within the Parish, or within some adjoining district, a generating station from which a proper and sufficient supply of energy would be given. The Company were also required to furnish the Vestry with a corrected plan of the works, with details. The plan 40 was submitted by the Company on the 26th July, 1898, and the Company proceeded with the work. System of Supply. In December, 1898, the Vestry received a communication from the Board of Trade enclosing letters from the Company, asking permission to change the system of supply to a system of two-phase alternating currents; the Vestry, however, did not agree to the proposal. Injunction against Company. In carrying out the work of laying mains throughout the parish, it was discovered by the Vestry's Surveyor that between Saturday, the 11th, and Monday, the 13th February, the Company laid down two sets of mains across Borough High Street, near St. George's Church. One of these sets of pipes was laid in the correct line, but the other was laid along a trench deviating from the plan in a south-westerly direction, from a point opposite St. George's Church to the southerly side of Marshalsea Eoad. The Company still insisting on laying pipes along the southerly side of that road, contrary to the plan, the Surveyor stopped the work on Thursday, the 16th February. The Company having claimed the right to lay pipes along the northerly and southerly sides of the road, beyond the point indicated on the plan, the Vestry Clerk was instructed, on the 17th February, to obtain an interim injunction restraining the Company from proceeding with the work. The case came before Mr. Justice Kennedy the next day, as an ex parte application, and he made an order restraining the Company from proceeding until the hearing of a summons before a Judge in Chambers. The case was heard by Mr. Justice Phillimore, on Friday, the 24th February, 1899, when, after reading the affidavits of the Vestry Clerk and Surveyor, and of the Assistant Engineer of the Company, and carefully examining the plan deposited by the Company with the Vestry, his lordship suggested that in his view it would be desirable for both parties to treat the hearing in Chambers as the trial of the action. The Company's Solicitor agreed to this course, and the Judge thereupon gave judgment for the Vestry for a declaration, 41 "That the Defendant Company have no right to break up the pavements or surface of Marshalsea Road, in the Parish of St. George the Martyr, Southwark, or to place electric mains and works in, under, along, or across such road otherwise than in accordance with the provisions of The Southwark Electric Lighting Order, 1892, confirmed by The Electric Lighting Orders Confirmation (No. 5) Act, 1892." He also gave judgment in favour of the Vestry for costs against the Company. The Judge, however, directed that judgment should not be entered until Tuesday, the 28th February, in order to give the Company an opportunity of then appearing, if on further consideration they were not prepared to consent to treat the hearing as the trial of the action. The Vestry Clerk subsequently received a letter from Mr. S. Morse, Solicitor to the Company, stating that he did not propose to appear on that day. Judgment was, therefore, drawn up and entered. Bill in Parliament. In the 1899 Session ot Parliament, the Company promoted a Bill, the practical effect of which was to enable them to construct three or four large generating stations in various parts of the Metropolis, and to supply the Parishes for which they held Provisional Orders and other extensive areas with electricity by this means. The Bill also sought to empower the Company to lay down connecting wires through Parishes, for which they already possessed an Order, but beyond the limits of the area of supply. After considering the whole measure the Vestry deemed it advisable to present a petition against the Bill. The Bill came before the Committee of the House of Commons on the 21st March; but a large number of local authorities, together with the County Council and numerous other Companies and persons were represented in opposition to the measure. The Vestry appeared by counsel, and after an hearing extending over seven days the Bill was thrown out by the Committee. generating stations and supply of electrical energy. A communication was received from the Vestry of Hammersmith, asking this Vestry to support the views of that Authority with regard 42 to certain suggestions contained in the Report of the Joint Committee of both Houses of Parliament on the subject. After considering the suggestions, the Vestry passed a resolution concurring with the views of Hammersmith, that, where powers have been given for the erection of a generating station outside the area of supply, the Local Authority within the area of supply should have the power of deciding the route the mains are to be laid, as well as the power of themselves breaking up and reinstating the streets. The Vestry also strongly objected to the proposals contained in the report to minimise the power of veto possessed by local authorities as to the erection of overhead wires and the granting of Electric Light Provisional Orders. Officers. vestry clerk's department. Mr. Arthur E. Baldrey was, on the 24th May, 1898, appointed Clerk in the Accountant's Department of the Vestry Clerk's Office, in the place of Mr. F. Seabrook, resigned, at a salary of 35s. per week, rising, by annual increments of 2s. 6d., to a maximum of 45s. a week. Owing to circumstances which are well known to the Vestry and the Parish, the Collector for Ward 1 was on the 12th July, 1898, on the recommendation of the Overseers, removed from his office, and Mr. Thomas Brown, the Vestry's Accountant, was ultimately appointed to the post on the 15th November, 1898. His poundage was fixed at the rate of 2½d. in the £ until the sum amounted to £300 per annum; after that sum was reached, the poundage on all monies collected to be at the rate of l½d. in the £. The position of Accountant was filled by the appointment of Mr. C. H. Patterson, A.S.A.A., on the 20th December, 1898, at the salary of £200 per annum, rising by annual increments of £10 to £250 per annum. Mr. V. A. Balls, Minute Clerk, resigned his post on the 21st March, 1899, on obtaining another appointment. surveyor's department. Mr. O. E. Winter, who had been Surveyor to the Parish from 1895, having obtained another appointment, handed his resignation 43 to the Vestry on the 12th July, 1898, and on the 26th July Mr. Arthur Harrison, A.M.I.C.E., was appointed Surveyor to the Vestry at the salary of £300 per annum, rising by annual increments of £25 to £450 per annum. On the 4th October, 1899, the Vestry determined to appoint an Assistant Surveyor, and advertisement were issued, for applicants for the post. The salary was fixed at £130 per annum, rising, by annual increments of £10, to a maximum of £180 per annum, and on the 29th November, 1898, Mr. R. T. Miller was appointed to the post. public health department. Mr. C. Grover, having resigned his appointment as Clerk in the Public Health Department, Mr. E. H. Thomas, of Swansea, was appointed to the position on the 28th June, 1898, at a salary of 35s. per week, rising, by annual increments of 2s. 6d., to a maximum of 40s. per week. The previous Caretakers of the Reception House having resigned, Mr. and Mrs. Aylmer were appointed by the Public Health Committee to succeed them (the former to act also as Superintendent of the Disinfecting Department), at the wages of 30s. per week, rising, by annual increments of 2s. 6d., to a maximum of 35s. per week, with an additional bonus of 2s. 6d. for each family received into the Reception House. The latter amount was increased, on the 21st March, 1899, to 5s. a family. On the 4th of October, 1898, Mr. Philip David was appointed as Sanitary Inspector for Ward No. 3, in place of Mr. W. H. Ralph, who had obtained another appointment. On the 18th October, 1898, the Vestry passed a resolution to the effect that in all official appointments made by the Vestry, any application made by an employee of the Vestry for such appointment shall receive special consideration of the Committee of selection. By order of the Vestry, J. A. JOHNSON, Vestry Clerk. July, 1899. VESTRY OF The Parish of St. George the Martyr, Southwark. ANNUAL REPORTS Of The Surveyor, FOR THE Year Ending March 25th, 1899. ARTHUR HARRISON, A.M. Inst., C.E., Surveyor. SURVEYOR'S ANNUAL REPORT. FOR THE YEAR ENDING MARCH 25TH, 1899. TO THE CHAIRMAN AND MEMBERS OF THE VESTRY. Ladies and Gentlemen, I beg to submit the following Report and Statement of the works executed under the supervision of my Department during the 12 months ending 25th March, 1899. ROADS AND FOOTWAYS. The works carried out under this head during the year have been generally in the character of repairs, with the exception of the wood paving opposite the Free Library, which was repaved in February with Jarrah blocks. The wood block paving has also been repaired in Borough High Street, Old Kent Road, and London Road. Repairs have been carried out to the sett paying in New Kent Road, Southwark Bridge Road, Newington Causeway, Page's Walk, Marshalsea Road, Tennis Court, Collier's Rent, Valentine Place, &c. Several streets which join Old Kent Road, and were in a dangerous condition, through the sharp dip at the crossings, have been re-laid, so that the roads now properly intersect. In paving and re-laying the above carriageways the following materials have been used:— REPAIRING WOOD AND SETT CARRIAGEWAYS. 109 ft. run Granite Channel. 23 gallons Tar. 470½ yds. super Old Granite Setts. 31 cwt. Pitch. 4½ cube yds. Sett Breakers. 34 ,, Coke. 65 ,, Pit Ballast. 7,866 new Jarrah Blocks. 89½ „ Sharp Sand. 290 old Jarrah Blocks. 69 „ Thames Ballast. 8½ lbs. Cotton Waste. 3 „ Old Concrete. 24 yds. Lamp Cotton. 713 sacks Cement. 25½ gallons Colza Oil. 60 gallons Creosote. 48 The repairs to the macadam carriageways during the year have been kept as low as possible, it being the intention in this district to do away with macadam as a carriageway material, and substituting either asphalte or granite sett paving, according to the circumstances of the case. Macadam, although recognised as a good and ready material for some situations, is most unsuitable for a district which is so completely built up as is this district. The Committee have already given orders in several cases for macadam roads and courts to be asphalted or paved, and the works are now in hand. After several of these works had been completed, the County of London and Brush Provincial Electric Lighting Co., commenced the work of laying then mains in the parish, which necessitated their opening the footpaths, after that no further work was carried out in the streets 49 that would be so disturbed, but asphalte footways in Potier Street and Belvedere Place were relaid, being dealt with as ordinary repairs. The York or flag footways have been repaired or relaid in St. George's Road near to the Cathedral, Newington Butts, Borough High Street, Old Kent Road, Little Hunter Street, Kell Street, Earl Street, Library Street, besides other streets that have been partially dealt with in connection with the trenches. The Trench work during the year has been very heavy, and our ordinary staff for repairs had to be considerably strengthened to meet the work in hand, as large trenches have been made in all the main thoroughfares of the Parish. South Metropolitan Gas Co. 501 Southwark and Vauxball Water Co. 232 Lambeth Water Works Co. 243 Gas Light & Coke Co. 55 London Electric Supply Corporation 35 London Hydraulic Power Co. 1 Post Office Telegraphs 2 County of London and Brush Provincial Electric Lighting Co. 5 1085 53 SEWERAGE. A commencement was made on the 5th of September to take out the old sewers in the Friar Street Area, and to lay new sewers in accordance with the scheme prepared by my predecessor, and up to date the following streets have been dealt with:—Friar Street, Lancaster Street, King James Street, Silex Street, Belvedere Buildings, Bean Street, and Minor Place; and those in Gun Street and Miniver Street are in progress. Earlier in the year, the old sewers were taken out and new sewers constructed in Little Suffolk Street, Sterry Street, and a portion in Borough Road. In carrying out this work, it was found that the original sewers had been laid with little regard to either line or level, and that jointing material had in many cases been forgotten or of such poor substance that it had disappeared. At the beginning of March, the sewer in Falstaff Yard was found to be in a very defective condition, and at the order of the Vestry this sewer was relaid. A number of combined drains have been relaid in various parts of the parish. The number of street gullies in the various streets is very low, and there is often a difficulty, in draining the water from the surface of the road. If these were increased, considerable saving in the weight of slop taken to the shoot would result, besides keeping the streets in a better condition. As a result of constant reports to the Sanitary Committee, of various sewers being unventilated, &c., the Committee have instructed your Surveyor to have a survey of the sewers in the parish, with a view to getting a correct plan of the existing sewers, and that the Surveyor prepare a report upon their condition, &c. This work is now in progress, and I hope in a short time to be in a position to submit a report on one portion of the parish. Deal. 3893 ,, l¼in. by 9in. ,, 10 ,, 1in. by 6in. ,, PRIVATE SEWER AND DRAINAGE WORK. In April a deposit of £492 3s. 0d. was received from Mr. R. J. Dickins, on behalf of Lord Llangattock, the estimated cost of the construction of a sewer in Searles Road, a new street which is being laid out behind the Paragon. So far, about half of the work has been carried out, it having to be done in sections on account of the amount of building material on the site. During the year 39 new frontage drains and 28 private drains have been cleared, relaid, or repaired. The following materials were used for this work :— 1 yd. Two new watch-boxes have been built, and one hand truck completed. HORSES. Your horses have been kept in good condition; there has been no serious illness, and the loss of work by the horses has been very small. 1 am also pleased to report that four of your drivers who paraded with their horses at Regent's Park, each received a first prize at the London Cart-horse Parade on Whit Monday. The Vestry have at various times provided temporary assistance in this department; but as the amount of work continued to increase, your Surveyor, early in September, submitted to the Works and Sewers Committee a report advising that a permanent professional assistant should be appointed; this, after due consideration, was decided upon, and in November the Vestry appointed Mr. Robt.
